    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="N.W. Moors" class="user" itemprop="url" name="N.W. Moors" href="/user/show/40847887-n-w-moors">N.W. Moors</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2668809283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5760116206626943659">Julia has moved to the small town of Smithville with her dog Ringo. She's looking for a place to hide after a serious illness that's left her debilitated but soon finds that small towns aren't good for being left alone. For starters, local deliveryman Chad has an eye on her as well as his employee Bobby and a mysterious black and white cat. But Chad has issues of his own that brought him back to town, and Julia's complications aren't what he wants - or does he?<br/>This is a lovely story about recove</span>
  <span id="freeText5760116206626943659" style="display:none">Julia has moved to the small town of Smithville with her dog Ringo. She's looking for a place to hide after a serious illness that's left her debilitated but soon finds that small towns aren't good for being left alone. For starters, local deliveryman Chad has an eye on her as well as his employee Bobby and a mysterious black and white cat. But Chad has issues of his own that brought him back to town, and Julia's complications aren't what he wants - or does he?<br />This is a lovely story about recovering from illness after losing everything and finding a home. I especially liked the author's characterization of Julia who can be depressed and ornery but is still likable as she finds her true self while not losing the steel that imbued her former personality. Chad's a nice guy who takes care of others but has been a bit lost and finds his true home in Julia.<br />There are some funny incidents that made me laugh out loud but fit into the story well. I can relate to George's 'illness' as I had the same thing happen in my past. <br />I recommend a visit to Smithville; you won't regret it.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5760116206626943659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2680975920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5204958742293121782">Smithville is the new home for Julia, who, after a devastating illness, finds herself divorced when her husband doesn't care for her anymore. In this small town, she finds peace with herself and her illness through gardening and restoring the dilapidate house she buys. Julia is a character in ..........'s first book, now her own story is told in the pages of Hometown Girl After All. Hometown Girl After All is an uplifting,old fashioned romance that will make you feel good inside.<br/>It is a lovely t</span>
  <span id="freeText5204958742293121782" style="display:none">Smithville is the new home for Julia, who, after a devastating illness, finds herself divorced when her husband doesn't care for her anymore. In this small town, she finds peace with herself and her illness through gardening and restoring the dilapidate house she buys. Julia is a character in ..........'s first book, now her own story is told in the pages of Hometown Girl After All. Hometown Girl After All is an uplifting,old fashioned romance that will make you feel good inside.<br />It is a lovely tale of new beginnings, the wrong people leaving our lives and happy endings. The writing flows smoothly from one scene to the next and from the first book to this one. This book is "stand alone" and can be read separately from the first one as I did. It makes great reading for a cold night or on the beach. Romance lovers everywhere will enjoy it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2914523135075876427"><strong>A very warm story</strong><br/><br/>A tough attorney suffered 6 months of a serious health setback when she had encephalitis. Her husband left her, saying she was no longer the woman he married. She bought an old dilapidated house without seeing it and drove across the country to her new home. She soon began restoring both the house and her strength as she gardened. A new life opened up. She found a caring community and love and acceptance.<br/>I liked the length of the story. Many stories end abruptly leaving readers </span>
  <span id="freeText2914523135075876427" style="display:none"><strong>A very warm story</strong><br /><br />A tough attorney suffered 6 months of a serious health setback when she had encephalitis. Her husband left her, saying she was no longer the woman he married. She bought an old dilapidated house without seeing it and drove across the country to her new home. She soon began restoring both the house and her strength as she gardened. A new life opened up. She found a caring community and love and acceptance.<br />I liked the length of the story. Many stories end abruptly leaving readers hanging, not sure what happened. Most unsatisfactory.<br />This gentle story continued to a satisfying conclusion. Lovely.</span>

<div id="review_3509852707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3509852707" />
    <a title="Kathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545016-kathy"><img alt="Kathy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3509852707?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/52545016-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3509852707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13517423495230109829">I am loving this series! Julia moves to town for a new start, after 6 weeks of illness caused her to lose everything, including her sense of self. But to her surprise, a small town is not a good place to hide away. People keep talking to her, visiting and won’t let her hide. This was a beautiful story, and so informative about encephalitis and how it affects a person. Chad was patient with her after she explained, and their relationship was up and down and so real. Ready for #3!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3274587910" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17589778769825291115"><strong>A new town, a new life? </strong><br/><br/>This is a new favorite author of mine! This book was superb! Julia wanted to make a fresh start where no one knew her. She chose the town of Smithville to move to to start her new life. She had been sick a long time & didn’t want people to judge her. She didn’t take into account that news travels fast in small towns, but quickly learned just how fast! She made new friends quickly, & also had Chad finding reasons to see her, to help her in the house she had purchased. She </span>
  <span id="freeText17589778769825291115" style="display:none"><strong>A new town, a new life? </strong><br /><br />This is a new favorite author of mine! This book was superb! Julia wanted to make a fresh start where no one knew her. She chose the town of Smithville to move to to start her new life. She had been sick a long time &amp; didn’t want people to judge her. She didn’t take into account that news travels fast in small towns, but quickly learned just how fast! She made new friends quickly, &amp; also had Chad finding reasons to see her, to help her in the house she had purchased. She decides to open a floral shop in the home she purchased. Little by little she becomes entrenched in The lives of several Smithfield’s residents. Throughout all this time, she told people she didn’t used to be like this Julia. No one believed her, until a couple of her friends ended up in trouble! Can she still be the person her new friends liked? This book is a good book for anyone! I highly recommend it as a wonderful read!</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s2IZVxP17Ahs7kY8DdXyX7bIKtlhjS1Leg5g0AIv82joAlRzKGID5/cDx4Ylu2j8gnF10rFhlWylXsW038Tlfw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AmwfnKawc19cPPRg00AulAwx0VFeEkNE86ax/43E8iJZDFK4nSecsMfRddr7LrQ3OIiOWo7++2Ms9hSbUC/kNQ==')})
  }
//]]>

The Germanic tribes would associate for their common good, often meeting and forming up for offensive or defensive war, but they were always separate and very independent. Armin knew that the best way to ensure that his country was not bothered by outside invaders again was to become a single country complete with it own army and navy. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11552913680849342304">Kirsten is a writer with a love of art and design. She worked in the engineering field, taught college, and consulted free lance. Due to health problems, she retired in 2012 to travel with her husband. They live and work full time in a 40' travel trailer with their little dog Bingo. Besides writing romance novels, she enjoys selling art on Etsy and spoiling their three grandchildren. <br/><br/>As a writer, </span>
  <span id="freeText11552913680849342304" style="display:none">Kirsten is a writer with a love of art and design. She worked in the engineering field, taught college, and consulted free lance. Due to health problems, she retired in 2012 to travel with her husband. They live and work full time in a 40' travel trailer with their little dog Bingo. Besides writing romance novels, she enjoys selling art on Etsy and spoiling their three grandchildren. <br /><br />As a writer, Kirsten's goal is to create strong female characters who face challenging, painful, and sometimes comical situations. She believes that the best way to deal with struggle is through friendship and women helping women. She knows good stories are based on interesting and relatable characters.</span>
